1 General 
1.1 Instructions for using the Operating Instructions for pumps 
(3.00.5600-001-en _Rev.02) 
1.1.1 Introduction 
In their design and manufacture, Rheinhütte pumps meet the high demands which are made on them in 
a wide variety of applications. Trouble-free operation of the pumps requires them to be properly used 
and handled in strict compliance with the operating instructions provided. Anyone entrusted by the user 
with the assembly, the installation, the operation, the servicing and the maintenance of Rheinhütte-
pumps (simply referred to as pumps in the following) must have read and understood the operating 
instructions, with particular reference to the "Safety" section. 
The operating instructions must always be available to these personnel. 
Only compliance and familiarity with these operating instructions can prevent mal -functioning of the 
pumps and ensure trouble-free operation. It is thus very important that these operating instructions are 
read and understood by the persons responsible and are strictly adhered to by those persons. 
We provide warranty for the pump in accordance with our Terms of Sale and Delivery insofar as the 
pump is used in coformity with ist intended use. All claims to warranty are null and void too, if damage 
is caused by incorrect operation, repairs or interference by persons who are not authorised to do so, 
and also if accessories and spare parts are used which are not specifically intended for use with our 
pumps. 
For further technical advice please contact our Customer Service Department or our Spares 
Department or one of our agents, who will be glad to help you. 
1.1.2 Area of application and purpose of use 
The pumps described in the Operating Instructions must only be operated in the areas of application 
specified in the Data Sheet. Limitations placed on their use must be complied with. Any other use will 
be construed as contravening the directions. If the specified application changes, authorisation for this 
should be obtained from Rheinhütte Pumpen GmbH, as otherwise the warranty becomes invalid. All 
claims for restitution will be null and void if this directive is not adhered to. 
The operating instructions mainly refer to the pump itself; and do on no account replace the 
documentation on accessories and / or peripherical components, e.g. motors, couplings, 
V-belt drives, devices for operating and / or control, thermosiphon pressure vessels etc. 
The pictures used in this operating instructions are meant as sustainment and, 
for reasons of simplicity, are only symbolic drawings.

1.2 Safety 
(Solar3.00.5602-001-en-Rev.00) 
1.2.1 General 
These Operating Instructions contain fundamental instructions which must be observed during installation, 
operation and maintenance. For this reason these Operating Instructions must always be read before assembly 
and commissioning by the fitter and also by the specialists / operators responsible, and must always be available at 
the site of the machine/installation. 
It is not only the general safety instructions listed under this main heading of Safety which need to be observed, but 
also the special safety instructions inserted into the sections which follow, such as for example personal practice. 
1.2.2 Marking of information 
Those safety instructions contained in these Operating Instructions which can endanger people if not adhered to 
are specially identified with the general danger symbol 
 
and for a warning of electrical voltage specially identified with 
 
For safety instructions whose non-observance can cause risks for the machine and its functioning, the word 
 
is inserted.

Instructions and/or instructions / warning notices put directly on the machine, such as

- Marking for fluid connections 
- Warning notice "Hot surfaces“

must be obeyed without fail and maintained in a fully readable condition. 
 
1.2.3 Qualification and Training of Personnel 
The personnel who will be operating, maintaining, inspecting and fitting must possess correct qualification for these 
tasks. Range of responsibility, accountability and monitoring of personnel mut be precisely determined the user. If 
there is not the required skill among the personnel, they must be trained and instructed. This can, if necessary, be 
done by the manufacturer/supplier of the equipment on behalf of the user. In addition the user should ensure the 
the content of the Operating Instructions is fully understood by the personnel. 
Note: 
The requirements for authorised personnel are regulated by the Technical Rules for Industrial Safety (TRBS 
1203, among others) in Germany. 
1.2.4 Dangers from non-compliance with the safety instructions 
Non-compliance with the safety instructions can have the consequences of endangering both the personnel and 
also the environment and the machine. Non-observance of the safety instructions can lead to the loss of any claims 
for damages. 
In detail non-compliance can, for example, carry the following risks: 
- Failure of important functions of the machine/plant 
- Incorrect methods of maintenance and upkeep 
- Endangerment of personnel due to electrical, mechanical and chemical risks 
- Risks to the environment dur to the escape of hazardous materials 
1.2.5 Safety-conscious working 
The safety instructions listed in these Operating 
Instructions, prevailing national regulations for accident prevention, and any user's internal working, operating and 
safety regulations must be adhered to.

1.2.6 Safety instructions for the user/operator 
- If any hot or cold parts of the machinery present a danger, they must be protected on site 
against being touched. 
- Anti-contact guards for moving parts (e.g. couplings) must not be removed from machines 
wich are in operation 
- leakage (e.g. at the shaft seal) of hazardous media (e.g. explosive, toxic, hot) must be 
removed in such a way that there is no risk to personnel or to the environment. Statutory 
regulations must be adhered to. 
- Risks from electricity must be prevented (for details of this see, for example, 
VDE Regulations, and the local electricity company regulations. 
1.2.7 Safety instructions for maintenance, inspection and fitting operations 
The user must ensure that all maintenance, inspection and fitting work is carried out by authorised and qualified 
specialist personnel, who have adequately prepared themselves by thorough study of the Operating Instructions. 
As a basic rule work on the machinery is only to be carried out with the machinery stopped. The procedures 
decribed in the Operating Instructions for stopping the machine must always be adhered to. 
Pumps or units which handle media hazardous to health must be decontaminated. 
Immediately after completing work, all safety and protective equipment must be replaced and/or m ade functional 
again. 
Before putting back into operation the points listed in the Section - Initial Commissioning - must be observed. 
1.2.8 Unauthorised modification and manufacture of spares 
Modification or alteration to the machine are permissible only after discussion with the manufacturer. Use of 
genuine spare parts and accessories authorised by the manufacturer is in the interests of safety. The use of other 
parts could invalidate all liability for the ensueing consequences. 
1.2.9 Prohibited methods of operation 
The operating safety of the machine supplied is guaranteed only if used in accordance with the specifications laid 
down in Section 1 of the Operating Instructions. The limits given in the data Sheet must on no account be 
exceeded.

The information and instructions given below are intended on the one hand to ensure the safety of

can be found on the packaging. Care must also be taken to see that the lifting gear (rope / cable etc.) is 
not pinched or crushed or otherwise damaged when lifting the goods !

equipment (ropes / cables, chains etc.) must also be observed!

2.1.1 General 
During the transportation and storage of vertical pumps or complete assemblies 
the pumps must be handled with particular care. 
2.1.2 Methods of Packaging 
RHEINHÜTTE pumps are packed in boxes or crates at the factory so that under normal transportation 
conditions damage will not occur. The particular type of transport (by land, by sea, by air) is always 
taken into account. 
• Normal packaging for despatch by land: 
Sturdy crates or boxes. 
• Normal packaging for despatch by sea: 
Sturdy wooden boxes lined with sand-free tar paper. 
The pumps should remain in the packaging during storage. 
• Sea packaging with plastic bag and desiccant: 
Sturdy wooden boxes lined with sand-free tar paper. 
The pumps are packed into sealed plastic bags under a partial vacuum. In the plastic bags there are 
small bags of desiccant compound. 
Note 1: 
For short term storage (up to 3 months) the packaging should neither be opened nor removed 
provided that it is undamaged. 
Note 2: 
If the packaging is unopened and undamaged the Storage and Maintenan ce Instructions do not 
come into effect until after > 3 months

illustrations below)!

2.1.4 Storage 
Please note that all the instructions on storage refer only to the pump! 
The instructions regarding the storage of other purchased parts (e.g. motor, mechanical seals, thermo -
siphon equipment, etc.) must also be complied with! 
2.1.4.1 Requirements for the storage area: 
• The pumps must be stored in a frost free place. 
• The storage area must be roofed over, dry and safe against flooding. 
• With closed rooms care should be taken to ensure that they are well ventilated. 
• “Pump / aggregate” must be protected against impact and shock loads, e.g.caused by 
 objects, tumbling down. 
2.1.4.2 Storage and Maintenance Instructions: 
• The storage-position is optimally, if corresponding to installation for operation; that means 
vertically and adequately supported at the sole plate of the delivery elbow. If vertically storage 
is impossible, the pumps must be stored in the horizontal position (lying down) and 
adequately supported. This means that pumps with a long submersion depth must be 
supported every 2m to prevent them from sagging. 
The pumps must also be adequately fixed in their location 
• All openings on the pump must be covered so that neither dust, water 
nor dirt can enter. 
• On metal pumps or plastic pumps having metal components in the hydraulic section of the 
pump (e.g. impeller, volute casing, suction cover etc.) the following additional maintenance 
instructions must also be complied with. 
1. Remove the covers from the suction and discharge nozzles every 4 - 8 weeks and 
check the pump visually for corrosion damage. 
2. Smear the sealing faces of the suction and discharge nozzles with a s uitable 
preservative. 
3 If possible, and permitted by the user, spray the hydraulic section of 
the pump through the suction and discharge nozzles with a suitable preservative 
which is compatible with the product and the material. 
Then reseal the suction and discharge nozzles. 
W A R N I N G: 
Comply with the instructions and warning notes from the manufacturer of the preservative! 
• For horizontal pumps: Check the pump about every 8 - 12 weeks for external corrosion 
damage and rotate the shaft 3 - 4 times by hand. 
For vertical pumps this time-interval is reduced up to 3 – 4 week. 
• On pumps which have gland packing and which have been in storage for longer than 3 
months, the gland packing should be removed and replaced with new packing material 
before the pump is put into operation, since the gland packings can deteriorate with 
age. 

[page 23]
RHEINHÜTTE Pumpen GmbH 
Rheingaustraße 96-98 
D-65203 Wiesbaden 
Tel. +49 611 604-0 Fax +49 611 604-328

• If it should turn out that a pump is being stored for a period of more than 5 years , the pump 
should be completely disassembled and checked for damage to individual components. 
 
 
If the pump is subject to excessive pollution during storage such as for example due 
to dust / dirt, aggressive vapours and/or the effects of severe weather etc., it should be 
completely disassembled after 3 years and checked for damage to individual 
components! 
Note 1: 
If there is any doubt when making the assessment RHEINHÜTTE should be informed 
or you should have the assessment carried out by RHEINHÜTTE Service! 
Both the lubricants in the anti-friction bearings and also the gaskets and sealing rings 
can be subject to changes depending on the resistance of the material to ageing and 
could adversely affect the operating safety of the pump. They should thus be 
replaced. 
The anti-friction bearings should be washed out, dried, inspected for damage and then 
refilled with the specified grease. 
Note 2: 
The necessary instructions regarding the lubrication of the bearings 
are attached to the Operating Instructions and must be complied with! 
Gasoline, petroleum spirits, dewatering fluids, neutral and alkaline aqueous cleaning 
fluids can be used for cleaning the anti-friction bearings. 
 
Dangers to health and risk of accidents when using the 
above cleaning agents! 
When using one of these cleaning agents the pump user 
must take all necessary measures to protect personnel! 
 
• Before putting the pump into operation all threaded fasteners (all nuts and bolts 
accessible from outside) must be checked and re-tightened in accordance with the 
document "Torque loadings for headless screws" attached to the Operating 
Instructions and if necessary also the document "Torque loadings for reduced shaft 
screws".

3 Product Description 
3.1 Type and design description – pump type: GVSO ...(“Molten Salt” - version ) 
(3.09.5100-002-Rev.05_EN) 
3.1.1 General: 
The RHEINHÜTTE vertical centrifugal pump type GVSO generally consists of a submerged tank pump 
(dry installation is possible to a limited extent. Please consult RHEINHÜTTE). The pump casing with 
double volute is normally (for wet installation) submerged in the liquid to be handled and is connected 
to the mounting flange by the suspension pipe. The pump is driven by a vertical flanged motor mounted 
on top of the motor stool. 
Depending on the pump size, the shaft is supported by one or more intermediate bearings (depending 
on the depth of submersion) for submersion depths greater than approx. 2200 mm. The column and 
suspension pipes consist of the discharge pipe (for the medium) and the shaft column. This means that 
the rotating shaft is not exposed to the flow. 
There are overflow holes in the upper part of the delivery suspension pipe which prevent the medium 
rising through the sleeve bearing gap from reaching the shaft entry. 
 
 
The overflow holes in the delivery suspension pipe should be above the level of 
the liquid in the tank at all times and be kept open! 
The shaft entry does not come into contact with the pumped medium. 
The support bearings in the volute and stage casing (for multi-stage pumps) and the intermediate 
bearings are lubricated by the pumped medium, provided this is free from solid particles. 
 
In this version (“Molten Salt” - version), the machine is not approved for use in 
gas-explosive atmospheres or dust-explosive atmospheres! 
3.1.2 Identification markings 
Each pump unit features a rating plate on the bearing 
bracket. The customer is advised to note the sales order 
number (R..) and serial number (P..) and to quote these in 
relation to all enquiries and when ordering spare parts from 
Rheinhütte. 
These numbers must be quoted in all correspondence and 
all orders for spare parts. 
 
Bild: Typenschild-01 

[page 25]
RHEINHÜTTE Pumpen GmbH 
Rheingaustraße 96-98 
D-65203 Wiesbaden 
Tel. +49 611 604-0 Fax +49 611 604-328 
Original OPERATING INSTRUCTIONS (BA) 
Attention: please specify in all correspondence our reference "R- and/or P-No" 
BA-GVSO...Molten_Salt_en-Rev.06.docx - Okt-2016 Page 20 of 88 
Datei : BA-GVSO...Molten_Salt_en-Rev.06.docx Druck : 21.10.16 Seiten : 88 
 
3.1.3 Design features: 
The design depicted is explained in the Technical Data Sheet describing the pump in detail. 
3.1.3.1 Shaft seal options 
In the case of molten salts, depending on the requirement, the following shaft sealing models come into 
the reckoning: 
Model A with stuffing box 
This type of sealing is used in pumps that are built in tanks, in the case of which there is a small 
differential pressure to the atmosphere, as well as for deployment against gasifying and fuming media. 
Between the packing rings, there is a locking ring, which can be charged, depending on the 
requirement, with compressed air or nitrogen (20 – 50 mbarg). The consumption is 60 – 80 Nl 
(standard litres) / min 
Design Y 
The shaft opening is sealed by one or several lip rings or by a pressurized carbon floating ring seal. 
This design can only be used if the shaft guide pipe is not subject to pressure. 
With a carbon floating ring seal, container pressures up to max. 4 bar can be sealed by air or nitrogen 
3.1.3.2 Direction of rotation 
The direction of rotation of the GVSO is anti-clockwise (to the left) when viewed from the drive end 
shaft stub. Exceptions are the pump sizes 200/400, 250/400 300/400, 400/500 und 450/500 which 
rotate in a clockwise direction (to the right) 
 
The drive unit should always be disconnected from the pump when checking 
the direction of rotation! 
The direction of rotation of the motor should correspond to that of the pump. 
Always check the direction arrow on the pump! 
3.1.3.3 Thrust bearing lantern 
Depending on the load (i.e. depending on the size and speed), the shaft is supported by one or two 
radial bearings in the thrust bearing lantern in the case of GVSO pumps. 
 
Under heavy pump operating conditions, the bearings have a 
nominal service life of 20,000 hours (assuming that the pump is 
operated correctly). 
Bearings are lubricated with grease. 
It is important that radial bearings are installed which have increased clearance corresponding to “C3”. 

[page 26]
RHEINHÜTTE Pumpen GmbH 
Rheingaustraße 96-98 
D-65203 Wiesbaden 
Tel. +49 611 604-0 Fax +49 611 604-328 
Original OPERATING INSTRUCTIONS (BA) 
Attention: please specify in all correspondence our reference "R- and/or P-No" 
BA-GVSO...Molten_Salt_en-Rev.06.docx - Okt-2016 Page 21 of 88 
Datei : BA-GVSO...Molten_Salt_en-Rev.06.docx Druck : 21.10.16 Seiten : 88 
 
3.1.3.4 Drive shaft 
Pumps with intermediate bearings have a split shaft. The joint of the shaft units and the transmission of 
the torque are achieved by means of a sleeve coupling which also acts as a shaft sleeve in the 
intermediate bearings. 
3.1.3.5 Mounting flange 
The mounting flange is circular, unless required in some other form. It is sealed with a gasket. The 
flange joining dimensions of the sole plate (144) as well as of the pressure pipe flange are defined in 
these cases on a case-to-case basis and should be taken from the dimensional arrangement drawing. 
The flange size indicated on the dimensional drawings (installation drawing) corresponds to the inside 
diameter. 
Corrosion resistant pumps usually have a plated mounting flange. 
3.1.3.6 Foot bearing, intermediate bearing 
In case of molten salts, the lubrication of the sleeve bearing is done by the transported material. 
Lubricant is applied via holes from the pressure pipe and the suspension tube filled with conveyed 
medium. 
3.1.3.7 Design for installation in tanks 
In this design the suction flange on the pump is not drilled. In the suspension pipe there are overflow 
holes through which the rising liquid drains back into the tank.

D-65203 Wiesbaden 
Tel. +49 611 604-0 Fax +49 611 604-328

3.2 Usage in conformity with intended purpose 
Solar3.00.5100-001-en-Rev.01 
RHEINHÜTTE pumps are selected and technically designed, on the basis of customer requirements/ orders, in 
keeping with the deployment and ambient conditions known to us, in such a way that safe operation of the relevant 
machine is ensured. In the framework of this design, the deployment boundaries are defined in the Technical Pump 
Data Sheet and together with the information and/or the restrictions provided in the operating manual, define the 
framework of the usage in conformity with intended purpose. 
Note: 
Inexact, missing or wrong data with reference to the deployment and ambient conditions can have an 
adverse effect on the accurate design of the pump, with regard to pump type, version and material 
selection. Damage owing to such information will have to be borne by the operator. 
Special sources of danger, such as ignition sources, do not generally occur when the usage is in conformity with 
intended purpose. The operator must take additional steps, which he must describe in his danger/risk analysis 
and/or his explosion protection document. 
 
 
Without previous discussion with and the consent of the manufacturer, the 
pump must never be operated outside of the agreed deployment and ambient 
conditions, since it and/or the pump module have been designed according to 
this agreed data. 
Note: 
Changing plant-specific or process-specific operations parameters can make 
an adjustment of the resultant pump design necessary, so that it is imperative 
to previously hold discussions with RHEINHÜTTE. 
Purpose-conformant use comprises, among other things, the following points; 
- Data on the medium to be pumped to the extent known to the manufacturer (see the data sheet) 
- Information on the delivery rate (see the data sheet) 
The pump may only be operated within the delivery rate limits "Qmin" (minimum permissible delivery rate) and 
"Qmax" (maximum permissible delivery rate). 
If no data sheet is available, you must contact the manufacturer without fail. 
- Operations data and usage limits (min. – / max specifications) of the pump/of the module with regard to 
pressure, medium and ambient temperature, rotational speed, transmissible power etc. (see the data sheet). 
- Max. noise intensity level (see data sheet and the corresponding explanations in the operating manual) 
- Data on shaft sealing and the their care as may be necessary (see the data sheet and the corresponding 
explanations in the operating manual) 
- Data on the antifriction bearing lubrication of the pump (see the data sheet and the corresponding 
explanations in the operating manual) 
- Information on the accessories and peripheral devices (see data sheet) 
- Starting up and shutting down procedure, such as data on the permissible degree of pump filling or level of the 
tank in the case of vertical pumps etc. (is treated in the operating manual) 
 
 
- Machines / pumps are operated only with all the protective devices in place e.g. coupling guards or belt 
guards. 
- Starting frequency of the module 
The starting frequency of the module is generally determined by the dimensioning of the motor and the joining 
elements between pump and motor (e.g. coupling). 
It thus depends to a great extent on its power reserves in stationary operation and the starting conditions 
(direct connection, star-delta, frequency-controlled operation, moment of inertia, etc.). 
The precondition for restarting of the pump is the previous 100% standstill of the pump rotor. 
When starting against a slightly opened pressure slider the following values can apply as guidelines. If these 
data are at variance from those of the motor and/or coupling element manufacturer, their data must also be

4 Setting-up and installation 
4.1 Instructions for the Initial Fitting of pumps vertical pumps into the Installation 
(Solar3.00.5106-001-en-Rev.00) 
The instructions and / or hints given in this chapter can only be a basic guide as the pump manufacturer 
is frequently not aware of the situation on site. 
If there are areas of uncertainty, queries or problems please contact RHEINHÜTTE Pumpen GmbH! 
 
 
The information and instructions given in this document are intended on the one 
hand to ensure the safety of personnel and third parties and on the other hand to 
safeguard the operating safety of the pump. They must be observed at all times. 
In all work carried out the generally accepted rules of the industry and the 
accident prevention regulations must always be adhered to. Local safety 
regulations always must be observed ! 
The section on Safety in the Operating Instructions must also be complied with! 
The pump user must take all necessary measures for the protection of personnel!

4.1.1 General 
Before installing the pump in the tank the protective covers on the flanges, pipes and over- 
flow holes, etc. need to be removed. 
The pump must be installed vertically. This means that the support flange of the pump must lean on the bearing 
suface of the tank/pit in a position as horizontal as possible. Alignment must be done by means of a suitable level 
to max. 1,0 mm/m. 
Note: 
The supporting surface for the level must be machined, plain and clean (e.g. support flange of the motor 
stool - bearing surface of the motor). 
To avoid vibration and running dry, the liquid must not be allowed to fall below the minimum level. 
Submersion dephts for wet installations can be incrased slightly by fitting an extension pipe (this must be discussed 
first with RHEINHÜTTE Pumpen GmbH). If the liquid level falls below the centre line of the impeller, it is obviously 
no longer possible to start up the pump when using this arrangement. When using a suction tube, care must be 
taken that the permissible suction head is not exceeded, in order to avoid cavitation. 
 
 
According the dimensional arrangement the minimum- or maximum-level 
of liquid must not be exceeded. 
The level has regularly to be controlled; if necessary install a monitoring device. 
In case of discharging the tank, a flowmeter at the discharge nozzle has to be 
provided. 
4.1.2 Details of the installation site 
Space requirements for operation and maintenance 
 
When planning the installation great care should be taken to ensure that there is sufficient space 
available around the pump to allow easy access for assembly and maintenance work. Any equipment 
connected before or after the pump should be arranged in similar fashion. 
 
In closed rooms the equipment should be installed so that there will be no build up of heat. Where 
ambient temperatures above 40 °C are expected suitable room ventilation must be provided to carry 
away the radiated heat and ensure a supply of fresh air. 
 
In order to avoid damages at the aggregate, the pump / aggregate must be protected against shock 
loadings, e.g. caused be objects, tumbling down. 

[page 31]

4.1.3 Piping 
General 
 
The size and routing of pump pipework is usually already specified at the design stage. 
Recommendations on the design of pipework can only be of a basic nature, allowing for the fact that 
the final design and layout of the piping will be carried out to suit the special situation on site, of which 
the pump manufacturer is frequently not aware. 
4.1.3.1 Tank Requirements 
Care must be taken to ensure that the distance from the bottom of the tank, and also from the tank 
walls is large enough to prevent disruption of the flow. If necessary this should be discussed with 
RHEINHÜTTE Pumpen GmbH. 
4.1.3.2 Discharge Pipes 
The inside diameter of the discharge piping should be the same as the rated size of the pump 
discharge connection or larger (in which case discussions should take place with RHEINHÜTTE 
Pumpen GmbH). A suitable isolating valve should be provided next to the pump, and this can be used 
to regulate the pump pressure and/or the flow rate. 
Recommendation: 
It is also recommended that a check valve or a non-return valve be installed between the isolating valve 
and the discharge nozzle to protect the pump and valves against shock loadings if the installation 
comes to a sudden stop.. 
If a pressure gauge is provided on the discharge side it must be fitted between the outlet connection 
(discharge nozzle) on the pump and the isolating valve (gate valve and / or non-return valve. 
4.1.3.3 Installation instructions for piping 
Only after the tank and piping have been thoroughly cleaned and all components precisely aligned, and 
the pump then fixed properly in position can the pipe(s) be connected. 
Once the pump has been connected to the pipe(s) no subsequent welding or alignment work 
can be carried out!! 

[page 32]
RHEINHÜTTE Pumpen GmbH 
Rheingaustraße 96-98 
D-65203 Wiesbaden 
Tel. +49 611 604-0 Fax +49 611 604-328 
Original OPERATING INSTRUCTIONS (BA) 
Attention: please specify in all correspondence our reference "R- and/or P-No" 
BA-GVSO...Molten_Salt_en-Rev.06.docx - Okt-2016 Page 27 of 88 
Datei : BA-GVSO...Molten_Salt_en-Rev.06.docx Druck : 21.10.16 Seiten : 88 
 
The pump must not act as a fixed point to take up the forces in the pipework. Changes in length in the 
pipes due to the effects of temperature must be compensated for by means of compensators, lyre 
bends, etc. 
The reaction forces from the deformation of these strain compensators must be taken up by special 
support points before the pump pressure connector. Compensators which are extended by internal 
pressure must be fitted with length restrictors and also properly adjusted. 
 
The pipes must never introduce loads onto the pump. 
No, or virtually no vibrations must be passed from the installation to the 
pump. 
The installation must, of course, be checked for leaks before being put into 
operation (pressure test or vacuum test as required).! 
4.1.4 Gaskets 
The gaskets must be of such a size and fixed in position so that under no circumstances can they foul 
the inside of the pipe and create adverse flow conditions for the pump. 
The gasket material must be completely suitable for the operating conditions in the installation. 
If the pumped medium and the gasket material permit it, the gaskets should be smeared with suitable 
grease (e.g. Graphite or PTFE grease).

Remark concerning this document: 
The images used in the present document are intended to provide assistance only and, for the sake of simplicity, 
are only symbolic representations. 
Only basic information can be provided in this document, because the pump manufacturer is generally unaware of 
the situation prevailing in the plant. 
In the event of lack of clarity, questions or problems, please contact RHEINHÜTTE. 
The information and instructions given below are intended to help ensure the safety of personnel and third parties 
as well as the operational safety of the pump, and are to be observed in every situation. 
 
The generally-recognized engineering rules and accident prevention 
regulations must be observed during all transportation work. 
Moreover, all relevant local and in-house safety regulations must always be 
complied with! 
In the case of the Federal Republic of Germany, these are, specifically, the 
administration regulations of the Berufsgenossenschaft or professional 
guilds (BGV). 
BGV A1 - General regulations 
BGV D8 - Lifting equipment 
BGV D6 - Cranes 
BGV A2 – Electrical systems and operating equipment 
BGR 104 – Explosion protection rules (Ex-RL) 
BGR 132 – Avoiding the danger of ignition from electrostatic charging 
It must be made sure that only approved sling and hoisting gear (cables, 
chains, braces, hoists, etc.) in perfect condition are used. Their load-bearing 
capacities must be sufficient to withstand the weight of the goods to be 
lifted. Moreover, it must be made sure that any lifting equipment (cables, 
etc.) is not crushed or otherwise damaged during lifting of the goods! 
In any case, the instructions by the lifting equipment manufacturer (e.g. for 
cables, chains, etc.) must be complied with. 
Please follow the safety instructions and any instructions provided by the 
manufacturer of the lifting gear. 
The hook of the crane must always be attached in such a way that the crane 
cable is vertical at any time, in order to prevent the freely-suspended load 
from slipping off and/or swinging. 
Persons must be kept away, without fail, from the swinging/ danger area of 
the pump during the lifting process. 
 
The safety information contained in the “Safety” chapter, as well as the 
statutory process-engineering and medium- and company-specific safety 
information are to be noted and observed. 
The owner is responsible for taking all the necessary measures to ensure that 
maintenance personnel, third parties and the environment are protected.

4.2.1 Pre-assembly of the steel structure / expansion joint 
The following subchapters are not relevant for direct installation into the tank (without using an expansion joint) 
and can therefore be skipped. 
4.2.1.1 Checking the steel structure and tank connection 
A It is reasonable to check that the central point of the steel structure matches the central point of the 
tank neck to avoid unnecessary crane movement. For this purpose you can use cords and a plummet. 
Of course, modern laser technology can also be used. 
Moreover, the distance between the steel structure and the tank neck and all dimensions for fastening 
of the lifting plate must be checked by means of the installation drawing. Checks also include distance 
and diameters of drilled holes, surface planarity and horizontal alignment of the tank flange and steel 
structure, which can be checked using a machine spirit level.

4.2.3 Lifting and errecting process of the pump 
For this process, two cranes are always required (e.g. a large, mobile telescopic crane and a truck crane) and, 
depending on the length of a pump, a pulley is required in order to connect two lifting points to the truck crane. For 
attachment to the sole plate, a crossbeam is always required. Take into account the weight as specified in the 
installation drawing. During the process, please make sure that the pump is suspended at all times and does not 
make contact with the floor. The pump must be lifted up a few metres in horizontal position before beginning with 
the errecting process. 
After tilting up the pump, it is only suspended by the big crane and can be positioned above the opening of the 
expansion joint.

4.2.5 Immersing the pump into the tank filled with hot molten salt (maintenance) 
Installation in this situation is performed according to the descriptions in section 1.4. 
However, the process is considerably more complicated, since the degrees of expansion of the individual 
components caused by the high temperature of the pumping medium differ significantly, which represents a great 
challenge. 
 
When using hot pumped media at temperatures > 200°C, the pumps have to be 
inserted into or drawn out of the material being conveyed very slowly (max. speed: 
0.05 m/min) to ensure that all heated pump sections can adjust to their ambient 
temperature (heat up or cool down) in a controlled manner. This ensures 
controlled expansion or contraction of the assemblies involved. If the cooling 
process for individual pump components is not sufficiently uniform, the pump will 
be damaged. 
Also, for immersion depths > 6 m, the “end bearing cover (361) / bearing housing 
(350)” threaded connection must be loosened; the shaft nut must be removed from 
the shaft and the shaft must be pushed forward to the end stop. This will allow 
relatively large differences in expansion between the shaft and the static components 
(pipes, housing, etc.) to be evened out. 
After completion of immersion and stabilisation of the expansion process (approx. 
24 hours) the pump must be correctly assembled and fixed. 
For this purpose, also see the document 
"Replacement of antifriction bearings with the pump installed - Type:GVSO 
(3.09.5698dm001)”. 
 
For such cases we recommend commissioning of specially trained Rheinhütte 
technicians to ensure best possible preparation and servicing of the pump for this 
process. In addition, for the drop downing process support and considerably more 
time is required to make sure that problems due to thermal expansion are ruled out 
throughout the entire process. 
 

[page 45]
RHEINHÜTTE Pumpen GmbH 
Rheingaustraße 96-98 
D-65203 Wiesbaden 
Tel. +49 611 604-0 Fax +49 611 604-328 
Original OPERATING INSTRUCTIONS (BA) 
Attention: please specify in all correspondence our reference "R- and/or P-No"

4.2.6 Installation of motor and coupling 
A Firstly, check that the coupling halves are correctly assembled to the pump and the motor, 
respectively. Subsequently, position the motor directly above the pump using suitable lifting equipment 
and drop down it until the motor is in correct position on the pump motor stool. During drop downing, 
we recommend inserting two screws into the motor flange to make sure that during drop down ing all 
holes are flush above one another. Also check the position of the terminal box during the process. If 
the motor is slightly inclined due to its centre of gravity, a pulley block can be used to tilt the motor into 
vertical position during drop downing.

4.2.7 Final assembly 
A after thoroughly cleaning the tubes and precisely aligning and properly fixing the pump in its position, 
the pipe(s) can be connected to the pump. 
Note: 
Please remember to insert the metal gasket between the counter flange and the pump flange 
before connecting the pipes. 
 
After establishing the connection(s) between the pump and the pipe(s), 
performance of subsequent welding or alignment work at the lines is prohibited! 
 
The pump must not act as a fixed point for forces associated with the piping . 
Changes in the length of the piping caused by temperature should be 
compensated for by means of expansion joints, Lyra bends, etc. The reaction 
forces arising from the deformation of these compensating elements have to be 
absorbed at special fixed points in front of the pump pressure nozzle. Expansion 
joints that will undergo expansion due to internal pressure, must be equipped 
with length limits and be correctly adjusted. 
 
The piping must not introduce any additional forces and/or moments into the 
pump due to installation conditions. 
It must be made sure that no or almost no vibration is transferred from the plant 
to the pump. 
 
 
 
 
It must be possible to install the 
flange tension-free

B Insulation at the expansion joint, lifting plate and pump pressure flange 
All insulation must be implemented by the plant owner, at the responsibility of the plant personnel. 
The same applies to the electrical heating for the output flange. 
For this purpose, the operating manuals of the pump and the expansion joint must be taken into 
account. 
The figure below only illustrates areas that need to or can be insulated; however, it does not provide 
information about the quality or thickness of the insulation. 
It is reasonable to use the same material as is intended for the other equipment, e.g. tanks, lines, etc. 
 
 
Danger of bearing overheat owing to insulation of the thrust bearing lantern. 
The insulation must be limited to the pipe elbow and the mounting plate at the most. 
The shaft passage and the bearing area must remain open towards the surroundings.

4.2.8 Dismantling the pump from the plant 
 
Pumps or individual parts of pumps can heat up due to process-engineering 
related factors or other physical influences. 
Burn hazard! 
A If present and necessary, remove the insulation on the mounting plate and the pipe elbow. 
Subsequently, all the supply pipes (e.g. for cooling medium, heating medium, barrier medium etc.) as 
well as any measurement / protection devices must be properly blocked off and/or made inoperable. 
The inner pressure that may be present in the supply pipes must be gradually equalised to the 
atmospheric pressure and the pipes separated from the pump. 
 
 
In order to counter the danger arising from the pipe or the contained 
medium, all necessary safety measures for protecting persons and the 
environment must be taken. 
In the case of pumps that are used for conveying hot media, (if permissible), 
the tank heating may only be shut off after the pulling of the pump. This 
helps to prevent the possible occurrence of premature solidification of the 
material (e.g. liquid sulphur, molten salts), so that the material being 
pumped can flow out of the pump as much as possible. 
B Loosen the screw joints of the pressure flange (if present) to the pump and support the pipes if 
required. 
C If present, remove the sun shade of the motor. 
Then, in the case of a detachable motor, the connection of the motor/motor stool as wel l as the 
connection of the motor/pump, if required, should be loosened. 
Subsequently, the motor is attached to the crane by the provided hoisting eyelets and carefully lifted off 
the pump. 

[page 50]
RHEINHÜTTE Pumpen GmbH 
Rheingaustraße 96-98 
D-65203 Wiesbaden 
Tel. +49 611 604-0 Fax +49 611 604-328

D Pulling and laying down the pump 
 
Please follow the safety instructions and any instructions provided by the 
manufacturer of the lifting gear. 
Use the lifting beam! 
The hook of the crane must always be attached in such a way that the crane 
cable is vertical at any time, in order to prevent the freely-suspended load 
from slipping off and/or swinging. 
Persons must be kept away, without fail, from the swinging/ danger area of 
the pump during the lifting process. 
 
Pumps with more than 1 intermediate bearing should generally be erected as 
well as laid down horizontally with two cranes. 
 
D1 Now loosen the connection between the machine/pump.If no lifting eyelets are present at the pump, 
screw ring bolts (lifting eyelets) in the threaded holes provided in the sole plate (893). Now, run the 
chain or the cable rope through the ring bolts. 
Note 1: 
When lifting and laying down the assembly "Pump/motor" care should be taken that neither the 
pump nor the motor is damaged by the lifting equipment (chain, cable...) (if required, use a 
suitable lifting beam). Only permissible for small and short pumps (without intermediate 
bearing). 
D2 Pull the pump out of the tank and after emptying it, swing it out of the opening area. 
Note 1: 
When using hot pumped media (temperature > 200°C), the pumps have to be drawn slowly from 
the material being conveyed (max. speed: 0.05 m/min), to ensure that all heated pump sections 
can cool down (and consequently contract) in a controlled manner. If the cooling process for 
individual pump components is not sufficiently uniform, the pump will be damaged. 
Also, for immersion depths > 6 m, the “End bearing cover (361) / bearing housing (350)” 
threaded connection is to be loosened. This will allow relatively large differences in expansion 
between the shaft and the static components (pipes, housing, etc.) to be evened out. 
Note 2: 
In the case of pumps that are supplied with a transport lock (see dimensional arrangement 
drawing), the lock should be put on again without fail before laying down the pump . 
 

[page 51]

4.2.9 Process for laying down the pump 
For this process, two cranes are always required (e.g. a large, mobile telescopic crane and a truck crane) and, 
depending on the length of a pump, a pulley is required in order to connect two lifting points to the truck crane. For 
attachment to the sole plate, a crossbeam is always required. Take into account the weight as specified in the 
installation drawing. During the process, please make sure that the pump is suspended at all times and does not 
make contact with the floor. The pump must be held suspended a few metres above ground until it is fully turned to 
horizontal position. 
Then, the pump must be carefully put down on the floor, secured against rolling, and supported with substructures 
in the area of the pump casing and the intermediate bearing to secure it against bending. 
Process without pulley (three lifting points)

4.3 Assembly and maintenance of flexible couplings 
(3.00.5131-003-en_Atex-Rev. 00_a) 
Note concerning this document: 
The indications and/or notes concerning assembly and maintenance of elastic couplings given in this document 
can only be of principal nature because the actual situation in the equipment is not known to the manufacturer of 
the pump most of the time. 
In case of uncertainties, questions or problems contact RHEINHÜTTE ! 
 
 
In order to be able to exclude an endangering because of electrical energy 
during works at the aggregate as well as the possibility of touching movable 
components the electrical energy supply to the drive motor as well as to 
possibly existing additional equipment of the pump has to be switched off 
beforehand and has to be secured against being switched on by error! 
(For corresponding details see for example the instructions of the VDE or of 
the local energy supplying enterprises) 
Principally works at the aggregate are only to be effected during standstill! 
4.3.1 Fitting the coupling halfs onto the pump shaft and motor shaft. 
 Before starting of the mounting the coupling halfs, pump and motor shaft ends are carefully to be 
burred, to be cleaned and very thinly to be coated with molybdenum disulphide (e. g. Molykote). 
Afterwards the keys have to be inserted into the provided grooves. 
 
With flexible couplings which consist of a hollow section and a claw section, 
the hollow section should always be fitted on the motor end. This will 
prevent articles of clothing being caught up on the protruding parts of the 
claw section if the motor is unintentionally started. 
 The coupling halfs on the side of the pump and on the side of the motor should, if possible, be pushed 
on by means of a special tool, so that the end of the shaft is flush with the hub of the coupling. If no 
special tool is available a steady warming up of the coupling halfs up to approx. 80°C facilitates the 
mounting. In this case the plastic buffers have to be removed before starting the warming up . 
 
During the assembly of the coupling it must be made sure that no axial 
shock load upon the anti-friction bearings of the pump and of the drive 
motor occurs!. 
 The axial securing of the coupling is effected by means of thread pins. These are tightened with an 
allen key (inbus key)according to DIN 911 without lengthening piece. 

[page 54]
RHEINHÜTTE Pumpen GmbH 
Rheingaustraße 96-98 
D-65203 Wiesbaden 
Tel. +49 611 604-0 Fax +49 611 604-328

4.3.2 Control of the rotation direction 
 
Under no circumstances the pump must be started / operated with the wrong 
direction of rotation! The rotation direction must be conform with the 
direction indicated by the arrow on the pump! 
- Control of the rotary field of the motor. 
For this it has to be observed that the rotary field of the motor refers to the end of the shaft of the motor. 
This means that for example a counter clockwise rotary field of the motor means a clockwise rotation of 
the pump. 
 
Before putting the pump and motor unit into operation 
always fit the coupling guard ! 
The accident prevention regulations only allow the pump to 
be operated with an anti-contact coupling guard fitted. 
4.3.3 Maintenance of elastic couplings 
The maintenance is restricted to a regular control of state (by inspection) of the elastic parts of the 
coupling which are subject to a certain natural wear. 
If a slight, however still admissible wear has been stated, the intervals of maintenance are to be 
shortened in accordance with the lifetime still to be expected of the wear parts. 
Note: 
In case considerable wear of the elastic parts of the coupling is stated these have to be 
replaced! 
Exact indications concerning the maintenance interval cannot be given because many different criteria 
(e.g. temperature influence at the coupling, acidity of the air of the surroundings, frequency of stopping 
and starting of the aggregate, damage of bearing at the pump and/or motor etc.) have an influence on 
the wear performance of the couplings. 
 

[page 55]

Tel. +49 611 604-0 Fax +49 611 604-328

4.4 Tightening torques for screws 
4.4.1 Tightness of the threaded connections 
(Solar3.09.5103-001-de-Rev. 02) 
 
The acceptable tightening torques listed in the following table should be 
considered only as very rough guidance values and as non-binding in nature. 
Always comply with the information given in the installation drawing and the 
technical pump data sheet, as well as the special information on tightening torques 
for screws (which has been added for special cases in the documentation). 
Any tightening torque values for screws stated there are binding in nature. 
The coefficient of sliding friction range, 0.12 µ - 0.14 µ, corresponds to a favourable 
surface (lubricated). 
The screws are to be tightened uniformly in a crosswise manner. 
Unless explicitly indicated otherwise, the screws are to be tightened in two or more 
steps. For “Siguss” and ceramic materials, it is essential to observe the 
20 – 40 – 60 – 80 Nm steps for the tightness. For metallic threaded connections, the 
screws are to be tightened in steps of 50 Nm.

4.4.3 Tightening torques for stretch bolts 
(3.00.5103-002-en_Atex-Rev. 04) 
 
The information contained in this chapter is intended to assist with the correct 
way of dealing with stretch bolts used on RHEINHÜTTE metal pumps. 
If anything is still unclear or if problems with stretch bolts are anticipated or 
even occur on our products, RHEINHÜTTE 
Div. Rheinhütte Pumpen should always be informed! 
Further activities, e.g. assembly, commissioning, should then be stopped unti l 
the matter is resolved! 
Introduction: 
If normal bolts are continually subjected to alternating loads they will break after some time as a result of fatigue 
even when they are adequately strongly designed. In these cases stretch bolts (resilient bolts) are much better able 
to withstand the loadings. Their shank diameter is only about 90% of the root diameter of the thread (0,9 x d3). 
The "necked", i.e. thinner, shank takes up the tensile stresses, which would otherwise overload the thread. 
Working alternately across the joint stretch bolts must be tightened / pre-stressed evenly within the elastic limit to 
specified figures (torque loadings) using a suitable torque wrench. 
A bolt is correctly tightened when it has been strained below the yield point, i.e. in the elastic zone of the bolt 
material. 
The pre-tension force acting on the bolt causes it to stretch, pressing the bolted components together. If the bolt is 
tightened too little the pre-tension force will be too low. This will allow the bolt to work loose. If it is properly 
tightened to just below the yield point, the pre-tension force will reach the right level. If the bolt is tightened too 
much it will be permanently overstrained and the pretension will be lower. Long bolts are less at risk because t hey 
can stretch more than short bolts. 
The torque applied when assembling a bolted joint must give a pre-tension force which is high enough to maintain 
the minimum clamping force when subject to operating forces. The pre-tension forces and torque loadings in the 
table are calculated so that the tensile stress in the cross section which matters (the cross sectional area of the 
stretch shank) together with the torsional stress which occurs when tightening reaches 90% of the 0,2% proof 
stress. 

[page 59]
RHEINHÜTTE Pumpen GmbH

D-65203 Wiesbaden 
Tel. +49 611 604-0 Fax +49 611 604-328

5.1.1 Introduction 
 
 
 
The safety instructions contained in the chapter "Safety" and the statutory 
safety regulations, instructions concerning process safety as well as safety 
instructions specific to the medium and company must be observed and 
complied with! 
The owner must take all precautions necessary to protect the maintenance 
personnel and other people, as well as the environment. 
 
 
 
In order to be able to exclude an endangering because of electrical energy 
during works at the aggregate as well as the possibility of touching movable 
components the electrical energy supply to the drive motor as well as to 
possibly existing additional equipment of the pump has to be switched off 
beforehand and has to be secured against being switched on by error! 
(For corresponding details see for example the instructions of the VDE or of the 
local energy supplying enterprises). 
Principally works at the aggregate are only to be effected during standstill! 
 

[page 63]

5.1.2 Measures and controls before putting pump into use 
The following measures and controls are to be effected: 
a In order to avoid an overstrain of the motor compare the nominal power of the motor with the power 
necessary to drive the pump. 
b All screw connections at the pump and the aggregate are to be controled with regard to tight seating 
and if necessary, are to be re-/tightened according to the specified initial torques for screws. 
c Control the initial torques of the connections of suction and discharge piping to the pump 
(if necessary tighten screw connections). 
d Various pump designs (shaft seal designs) have to be provided with flushing, seal and/or quench 
medium. For this it has to be checked whether the connections necessary for the medium/s are 
mounted correctly and whether the corresponding medium is provided with the specified pressure and 
in the specified quantity (in this context, see the corresponding chapter " Type descr iption - Pump type: 
GVSO \ Shaft sealing options ...."). 
e If control and/or provision equipment (Monitoring system, temperature gauge, protection against dry 
operation, block pressure devices and other) is provided the connections and their correct functi on 
have to be controled. 
f Possibly existing measure devices (pressure gauge and other) have to be mounted correctly and their 
ranges of measurement have to correspond to the operating data of the pump. 
g The motor can now be connected to the power supply and the direction of rotation checked. 
Note: 
The necessary installation work may only be carried out by duly authorized qualified personnel with due 
regard for all applicable statutory regulations, process safety instructions, and specific safety 
instructions relating to the medium, plant and company. 
h Pumps which are to be used to convey hot media, before further flooding and/or being put into 
operation, must be warmed thoroughly. This means that the temperature at the pump (in particular, 
around the shaft guide, e.g. at the shaft, shaft guide tubes and intermediate bearing) corresponds to 
the temperature of the conveying medium. The warming duration (at least 12 hours) has to be selected 
accordingly. 
Note: RHEINHÜTTE is always available to answer any questions and resolve any issues. 

[page 64]
RHEINHÜTTE Pumpen GmbH 
Rheingaustraße 96-98 
D-65203 Wiesbaden 
Tel. +49 611 604-0 Fax +49 611 604-328 
Original OPERATING INSTRUCTIONS (BA) 
Attention: please specify in all correspondence our reference "R- and/or P-No" 
BA-GVSO...Molten_Salt_en-Rev.06.docx - Okt-2016 Page 59 of 88 
Datei : BA-GVSO...Molten_Salt_en-Rev.06.docx Druck : 21.10.16 Seiten : 88 
 
i Field-testing the motor. 
It should be noted in this case that the rotary field of the motor refers to the shaft end of the motor. This 
means, for instance, that left-hand rotation by the motor is equivalent to right-hand rotation by the 
pump. 
 
After checking the direction of rotation, the unit must be duly secured to prevent 
inadvertent start-up in order to protect the operating / service personnel until the 
coupling guard / guard against accidental contact can be properly fitted. 
j Check alignment of the motor / pump units (not applicable for flange-motor pumps): 
Note: 
The instructions in the corresponding chapters and/or operating manuals for couplings / V -belts must 
be observed! 
In the case of couplings which are not screwed together, the distance between the shaft ends of the 
motor and pump and between the two coupling halves must be checked. It must be equal to 5- 6 mm in 
each case. 
 
The shaft must then be turned by hand to check that the motor / pump unit moves easily before duly 
fitting the coupling guard / guard to prevent accidental contact. 
k In case of grease-lubricated anti friction bearings with separate supply of lubricant it 
has to be checked before start up that the supply is in working order. 
Note: 
The corresponding chapter concerning greasing of bearings and/or the operating instruction for the 
corresponding supply unit as well as the lubrication chart are to be observed! 
5.1.3 Start up 
 
The pump may only be operated within the Qmin-/ and Qmax limits in 
accordance with the Technical Pump Data Sheet and / or the pump 
characteristic. 
In the case of accompanying frequencytransformers (also supplied), the 
documentation of the frequency transformer additionally contains various 
brake curve diagrams of the entire power train of the pump assembly. 
a In case supervision / provision equipment etc. is used this has to be put into operation now. 
b When filling, slowly open the discharge-valve, to avoid an accumulation of air 

[page 65]
RHEINHÜTTE Pumpen GmbH 
Rheingaustraße 96-98 
D-65203 Wiesbaden 
Tel. +49 611 604-0 Fax +49 611 604-328 
Original OPERATING INSTRUCTIONS (BA) 
Attention: please specify in all correspondence our reference "R- and/or P-No" 
BA-GVSO...Molten_Salt_en-Rev.06.docx - Okt-2016 Page 60 of 88 
Datei : BA-GVSO...Molten_Salt_en-Rev.06.docx Druck : 21.10.16 Seiten : 88 
 
c Switch on motor 
Note: 
The ramp must be set to between 5s and 10s in frequency transformer mode. 
 
If 2 or more pumps are started in parallel, it is imperative to ensure identical 
rotational speeds of the pumps. 
h Immediately after the motor has been switched on the discharge valve has to be opened slowly until 
the specified transportation data (see type plate) is reached. 
5.1.4 Stopping the pump 
a Close the shutoff valve in the delivery line and switch off the motor. 
Note: 
The shutoff valve may remain open if a non-return check valve is installed in the delivery line. The 
pump will run backwards if the flow cannot be shut off. 
 
An unabated running backwards of the pump has to be avoided. 
This can - for example - cause vibrations and / or lacking lubrication and 
ensuing damages on the pump. 
In case of uncertainties contact the manufacturer! 
After the motor has been switched off the pump must slow down evenly. 
In case it stops all at once a fault has occurred which has to be examined and corrected without delay. 
Note: 
All supply and/or monitoring devices (e.g. for sealing, flushing, heating medium, etc.) must 
remain active until the pump has been drained! 
5.1.5 Restarting the pump 
In systems without non-return valves or other quick-closing shutoff fittings, it must be remembered that the pump 
will run in reverse due to the return flow of medium when the pump is switched off manually, during all -automatic or 
intermittent pump operation and in the event of a power failure. 
The duration of reverse running depends on the amount of medium flowing back. 
 
The pump must not be restarted until it has come to a complete halt!

5.1.6 Prohibited methods of operation 
a The pump must never be operated outside the agreed operating data without first consulting the 
manufacturer and without obtaining the latter's prior approval, as the pump and/or pump unit has/have 
been designed and built in accordance with these agreed data. 
Note: 
Changes in plant or process engineering parameters may make it necessary to adjust the 
resultant pump setting. RHEINHÜTTE must therefore be consulted beforehand without fail ! 
b A dry running of the pump has to be avoided by all means! 
c The pump must not be operated with the discharge valve closed! 
 
In certain circumstances starting the pump against a closed discharge valve is 
possible, if the maximum starting-time does not exceed 5 – 10 seconds. 
In case of uncertainties contact the manufacturer! 
5.1.7 Control during operation 
a Pump start-up phase must be monitored, max. starting time = 5-10 s (without consulting the 
manufacturer). 
b The unit pump - motor must run evenly and without vibrations. 
c The operating data are to be controled regularly. 
d The pump must be visually inspected for leaks. 
e All the monitoring, control and/or supply equipment (monitoring system for monitoring the pressure, 
temperature, rotational speed and vibration or controller for the blocking/ rinsing device of the shaft 
sealing system etc. must be continuously checked for their operability. A connection to a/the process 
control system is highly recommended. 
f The temperatures of the anti friction bearings and the surfaces must not exceed the permissible limits. 
g Relubrication intervals must be observed in the case of not incased, grease-lubricated anti-friction 
bearings.

6 Maintenance, inspections and disposal 
6.1 "Maintenance, inspection and their intervals“ 
Solar3.00.5198-001-en-Rev.02 
Introduction: 
The information that is given in this section is based on general guidance instructions and internal 
recommendations. The extent of inspection and maintenance as well as their intervals must be examined 
and if required, modified and/or extended by the owner/operator in accordance with the plant-specific and 
medium-specific conditions (temperature and weather influences, plant-caused vibrations etc.) as well as 
in particular reference to the danger to humans and machines originating from the me dium to be pumped. 
In any case, all the legal, process-engineering and medium-specific and company-specific safety 
instructions must be followed and complied with without fail. 
So also, compliance is required with the operating manuals of all the additional modules (e.g. motor, 
monitoring devices etc.) and the instructions that they contain. 
All the data with regard to inspection/ maintenance and their intervals assume a proper commissioning as 
well as fault-free operation of the plant and the pump module within the operation application as designed 
by us. 
Please consult RHEINHÜTTE in case of any doubts, questions or problems. 
 
A repair operation that makes pulling and dismantling of the pump necessary 
should not be carried out without consulting the manufacturer, since this 
may, among other things, make it necessary to use a steam blaster and/or 
oxyacetylene torch. 
 
6.1.1 Definition of terms according to IEC 60079-17: 
Maintenance and repair: 
A combination of all the activities that are carried out to maintain an object in a particular state or to 
restore it to that state, which (the state) conforms to the requirements of the relevant specification and 
ensures the execution of the required functions. 
Inspection: 
An activity carried out that includes careful examination of an object, with the goal of making a reliable 
statement about the state of that object, with the inspection being carried out without dismantling or, if 
required, with only partial dismantling, supplemented by other measures, such as measurements. 
Visual inspection: 
A visual inspection is an examination in which visible faults are determined, such as missing screws, 
without using additional devices or tools. 

[page 71]
RHEINHÜTTE Pumpen GmbH 
Rheingaustraße 96-98 
D-65203 Wiesbaden 
Tel. +49 611 604-0 Fax +49 611 604-328 
Original OPERATING INSTRUCTIONS (BA) 
Attention: please specify in all correspondence our reference "R- and/or P-No" 
BA-GVSO...Molten_Salt_en-Rev.06.docx - Okt-2016 Page 66 of 88 
Datei : BA-GVSO...Molten_Salt_en-Rev.06.docx Druck : 21.10.16 Seiten : 88 
 
Close inspection: 
An inspection in which in addition to the aspects of the visual inspection, such errors are determined, 
e.g. loose screws, which can only be detected by using auxiliary devices, e.g. steps (if required), and 
tools. For close inspections, a housing need not normally be opened or the operating equipment nee d 
not be rendered free of voltage. 
Detailed inspection: 
An inspection in which in addition to the aspects of the close inspection, such faults are determined, 
e.g. loose connections, which can only be detected by opening the cabinets and/or if required, using 
tools and testing equipment. 
• Upkeep procedures may only be carried out by RHEINHÜTTE personnel or personnel specially trained by 
RHEINHÜTTE. 
• Upkeep procedures involving dismantling the machine may only be carried out in an explosion- free 
atmosphere. 
• Components may only be exchanged for original spare parts, which also applies to the lubricants and 
auxiliary materials. 
• After maintenance and/or repair procedures, all the barriers and instructions that have been removed 
during the procedures must be restored to their original positions.

6.2 Tightening torques for screws 
6.2.1 Tightness of the threaded connections 
(Solar3.09.5103-001-de-Rev. 02) 
 
The acceptable tightening torques listed in the following table should be 
considered only as very rough guidance values and as non-binding in nature. 
Always comply with the information given in the installation drawing and the 
technical pump data sheet, as well as the special information on tightening torques 
for screws (which has been added for special cases in the documentation). 
Any tightening torque values for screws stated there are binding in nature. 
The coefficient of sliding friction range, 0.12 µ - 0.14 µ, corresponds to a favourable 
surface (lubricated). 
The screws are to be tightened uniformly in a crosswise manner. 
Unless explicitly indicated otherwise, the screws are to be tightened in two or more 
steps. For “Siguss” and ceramic materials, it is essential to observe the 
20 – 40 – 60 – 80 Nm steps for the tightness. For metallic threaded connections, the 
screws are to be tightened in steps of 50 Nm.

6.2.3 Tightening torques for stretch bolts 
(3.00.5103-002-en_Atex-Rev. 04) 
 
The information contained in this chapter is intended to assist with the correct 
way of dealing with stretch bolts used on RHEINHÜTTE metal pumps. 
If anything is still unclear or if problems with stretch bolts are anticipated or 
even occur on our products, RHEINHÜTTE 
Div. Rheinhütte Pumpen should always be informed! 
Further activities, e.g. assembly, commissioning, should then be stopped until 
the matter is resolved! 
Introduction: 
If normal bolts are continually subjected to alternating loads they will break after some time as a result of fatigue 
even when they are adequately strongly designed. In these cases stretch bolts (resilient bolts) are much better able 
to withstand the loadings. Their shank diameter is only about 90% of the root diameter of the thread (0,9 x d3). 
The "necked", i.e. thinner, shank takes up the tensile stresses, which would otherwise overload the thread. 
Working alternately across the joint stretch bolts must be tightened / pre-stressed evenly within the elastic limit to 
specified figures (torque loadings) using a suitable torque wrench. 
A bolt is correctly tightened when it has been strained below the yield point, i.e. in the elastic zone of the bolt 
material. 
The pre-tension force acting on the bolt causes it to stretch, pressing the bolted components together. If the bolt is 
tightened too little the pre-tension force will be too low. This will allow the bolt to work loose. If it is properly 
tightened to just below the yield point, the pre-tension force will reach the right level. If the bolt is tightened too 
much it will be permanently overstrained and the pretension will be lower. Long bolts are less at risk because they 
can stretch more than short bolts. 
The torque applied when assembling a bolted joint must give a pre-tension force which is high enough to maintain 
the minimum clamping force when subject to operating forces. The pre-tension forces and torque loadings in the 
table are calculated so that the tensile stress in the cross section which matters (the cross sectional area of the 
stretch shank) together with the torsional stress which occurs when tightening reaches 90% of the 0,2% proof 
stress.

6.5.2 Assembly Instructions for Stuffing-box Packing 
(3.00.5601-002_Rev.2-en) 
At the factory, RHEINHÜTTE pumps are fitted with pre-formed and dimensionally accurate packing rings. When 
replacing them, basically, only exactly matching packing thicknesses should be used. 
The thickness of a packing is calculated from: 
 
S = D - d 
2 
Fitting too strong or too weak packing would result in damage to the shaft sleeve and excessive power drawn or 
leaks. 
The packing rings assigned to a pump should be procured from RHEINHÜTTE Service as spare parts. 
The dimensions for this can be obtained from the attached parts list. 
1. Before installing new packing rings, the stuffing box must be cleaned of old packing residues. For 
dismantling old packings, the use of a flexible packing puller is recommended. 
2. Stuffing-box packing may never be fitted in spiral form, but only in individual rings. A straight cut 
should be used in the case of braided soft packing. 
3. However, if packing rings are to be cut to size from available material, the cut length is determined by 
the diameter of the shaft sleeve, with the following rule applying: 
 Length = 1.1 x π x dw (dw = diameter of the shaft sleeve) 
4. Place the individual cut packing rings in the packing space with the cut ends first and then gradually 
press them with a gland - never with a rod - on the ground till the stuffing box is full. The rings must be 
inserted with cut ends displaced by 90° each. 
5. The stuffing box gland should be put on and the screws or nuts tightened - not too tight, by hand as far 
as possible. 
 
 

[page 85]
RHEINHÜTTE Pumpen GmbH 
Rheingaustraße 96-98 
D-65203 Wiesbaden 
Tel. +49 611 604-0 Fax +49 611 604-328

6.6 Lubrication intervals and requirements for 
pumps with grease lubrication 
(3.00.5400-001-en_Atex-Rev.02) 
Horizontal RHEINHÜTTE pumps, whose anti-friction bearings are lubricated with grease, have greasing points 
(grease nipples) fitted as standard for regreasing 
For pumps whose bearings are continually greased through a lubricant feeder (e.g. the Perma-lubricator), the 
operating instructions from the manufacturer of the lubricator are included in the operating instructions from 
RHEINHÜTTE. 
The operating instructions from the manufacturer of the lubricator must always be complied with! 
The type of lubrication system fitted at the time of delivery as well as all necessary informations on the lubrication of 
the bearings is given in the Technical pump data sheet under the heading “specific informations on pump”. 
A selection of suitable greases of different producers can be found in our lubrication chart 3.00.5510. 
General information on the lubrication of grease lubricated anti-friction bearings: 
The grease in the anti-friction bearing is dispersed during the first running hours of the pump. In this 
period the bearing also performs a scouring action and distributes the grease evenly, thus forming a 
film of grease on the load bearing parts. 
This film of grease has the function of preventing metal to metal contact within the bearing, so that the 
running conditions of the anti-friction bearing are optimised. 
During this scouring action the energy put in by the work done is converted into heat by the friction 
which is generated 
After this initial period the bearing runs at only 30 to 50% of the starting friction. 
 
If the anti-friction bearing is overfilled with grease a great deal of frictional 
heat is generated by the very high scouring action which the bearing has to 
perform. 
The bearings could run hot and this can lead to bearing damage and hence 
to a breakdown of the pump. 
If using different greases always ensure that the types of grease are 
compatible with each other without restriction, as otherwise they could 
react with each other. This can have an adverse effect on their lubrication 
properties!

6.1 Disposal 
(3.00.5106-500-en_Atex-Rev.00) 
 
Disposal of the cleaned / decontaminated machine must take place in compliance 
with national and local regulations as part of the normal material process or by 
returning to the manufacturer. 
The following points should be noted during disposal: 
 Oils and greases must be disposed of properly in accordance with the German Waste Oils Ordinance. No 
mixing with solvents, cold cleaning agents or paint residues. 
 If possible and necessary, separate components for recycling by: 
- Electronic waste 
- Grey cast iron 
- Steel 
- Stainless steel 
- Light metals (sorted by type) 
- Non-ferrous metals (machine windings, worm gears) 
- Plastics (polyamide, glass fibre reinforced polyamide, polypropylene etc.) 
You can obtain more specific information about proper separation and recycling from your local waste disposal 
service or the relevant competent authority.

7 Possible malfunctions and their cure 
7.1 Possible operational malfunctions and their cure 
(Solar3.00.5106-008-en-Rev.01) 
Notes on this chapter: 
The details given in this chapter can only be of a general nature since the situation at the installation is 
usually not known to the pump manufacturer. 
In all cases the statutory safety instructions and also those relating to the process or the medium and 
those specific to the company must be observed and adhered to without fail! 
Likewise the operating instructions for all auxiliary equipment (e.g. the motor, the mo nitoring equipment 
etc.) must be observed and the directions contained in them must be followed! 
The pump must never be operated outside the agreed operating parameters without prior discussion with 
the manufacturer and only with his permission, since the pump and/or the pump and motor unit was 
designed in accordance with these agreed parameters. 
Note: 
Changes to the operating parameters of the plant or process could make it necessary to adjust the pump 
settings, so these should always be discussed with RHEINHÜTTE in advance! 
If there are areas of uncertainty, questions or problems please get in touch with RHEINHÜTTE !

7.1.6 Impermissible temperature rise in the pump / increased bearing temperature ! 
 
 
 
 
Impermissible temperature rises in/on the pump or unit indicate that the 
machine may be damaged and possibly lead to machine failure, as well as 
endangering people, animals and the environment. 
Particularly in explosion-hazard areas, care must be taken to ensure that the 
correspondingly specified temperature classes are not exceeded under any 
circumstances! 
In such cases, the unit must be switched off via the Emergency OFF function 
and safety ensured! 
The operating instructions for all supplementary units (e.g. motor, 
monitoring equipment, etc.) must also be observed and complied with! 
 
 Possible cause CURE 
A Pump runs against a closed shutoff valve Switch the unit off immediately. Ensure safety and 
examine the pump for signs of damage. Let it cool. 
Consult RHEINHÜTTE if necessary. 
B Pump runs dry Switch the unit off immediately. Ensure safety and 
examine the pump for signs of damage. Consult 
RHEINHÜTTE if necessary. 
C The actual operating parameters (geodetic 
delivery head, viscosity, specific gravity of 
the product being pumped, etc.) differ from 
those stated on the order. 
Consult RHEINHÜTTE! 
D The geodetic height or the frictional 
resistance of the pipe is greater than 
originally assumed. 
Install delivery pipes with a larger cross-section, increase 
the diameter of the impeller (if possible) or modify the 
installation. 
Consult RHEINHÜTTE! 
E Delivery rate too low Increase the minimum delivery rate

1 Replacing the Antifriction Bearings with the 
Inbuilt Pump - Type: GVSO 
3.09.5698dm001-en-Rev.05 
Note: 
The pictures and photographs used in this description are intended as aids only. They are not a 
replacement for the sectional drawing that is the basis of the assembly instructions. 
1.1 General Safety Instructions 
 
 
The safety instructions given in the chapter "Safety" as well as the legally 
prescribed safety instructions, the process engineering safety instructions 
as well as the medium-specific and company-specific safety instructions 
must be noted and followed. 
The owner/operator must take all the measures required for protecting the 
maintenance personnel and third parties as well as the environment. 
In explosive areas, compliance is additionally required with the 
corresponding applicable explosion protection regulations. 
So also, compliance is required with the operating manuals of all the add -on 
assemblies (for example, the motor, monitoring devices etc.) and all the 
instructions in them. 
 
 
To eliminate the possibility of a hazard from electrical energy when working 
with the machine as well as the possibility of touching movable components, 
the energy supply to the driving motor as well as any add-on devices that 
may be present at the pump should be switched off and secured from getting 
turned on accidentally. 
(For details regarding this, see e.g. the specifications of the VDE and the 
local energy supply companies) 
Basically, work on the machine should only be carried out when it is at 
standstill. 
 
In the case of pumps whose components were manufactured from a material 
(for example 1.4571, 1.4408 or the like) with a tendency to corrode (cold-
welding), extreme care must be taken when monitoring the parts as well as 
when dismantling / assembling them. 
The unnecessary use of force must always be avoided. 
To prevent cold-welding, the parts in the endangered area should be coated 
with a high pressure- resistant and heat-resistant anti-fusing agent (for 
example, THREAD - EZE) - if the material being pumped allows this. 
If the parts are difficult to fit, insert or screw together during fitting or 
assembly, the operation must be stopped immediately and the pressure point 
must be found and eliminated. 
 
Note: For the sake of simplicity, the product "THREAD-EZE" being used by Rheinhütte at the time of printing of this 
operating manual will be specified instead of "high pressure-resistant and heat-resistant anti-fusing agent". 

[page 108]
RHEINHÜTTE Pumpen GmbH 
Rheingaustraße 96-98 
D-65203 Wiesbaden 
Tel. +49 611 604-0 Fax +49 611 604-328

1.2 Dismantling the Drive-side Antifriction Bearings 
A Properly block off all the supply lines (for example, for coolant, heating medium, blocking medium etc.) 
as well as any measurement / protection devices, and render them inoperative. 
The inner pressure that may be present in the supply pipes must be gradually equalised to the 
atmospheric pressure and the pipes separated from the pump. 
B If present, remove the sun shade of the motor. 
Then, in the case of a detachable motor, the connection of the motor/motor stool as well as the 
connection of the motor/pump, if required, should be loosened. 
Then, the motor is suspended using the lifting hooks provided for the purpose from a crane and 
carefully lifted away from the pump. 

[page 109]
RHEINHÜTTE Pumpen GmbH 
Rheingaustraße 96-98 
D-65203 Wiesbaden 
Tel. +49 611 604-0 Fax +49 611 604-328 
 
 
3.09.5698dm001-en-Rev.05.docx 3 / 18 
 
 
File : 3.09.5698dm001-en-Rev.05.docx Print: 17.10.16 Pages : 18 
 
C Loosen the threaded joint of the motor stool (341) / thrust bearing lantern (342) and lift up the motor 
stool. Next, loosen the grub screw that secures the pump-side coupling half from axial displacement, 
and pull off the coupling half from the top shaft (213) using a suitable extractor. 
The key (213.940.0) should then be removed. 
 
D Dismantle the lubrication piping as well as the temperature sensor, if there is one.

key

and temperature sensors
